Oath on Impossible Act: The Condition of Possibility (Tassawur al-Birr)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on oath validity when fulfillment is impossible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition of possibility for oath validity and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
An oath requires possibility of fulfillment; if impossible from the start, the oath never contracts.

This passage examines a classical case: a man swears to drink water from a specific jug, but the jug is empty or the water is spilled. Does he break his oath? The Hanafi school is split on the requirement that the sworn act be possible. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad insist on 'tassawur al-birr' — the oath must be conceivably fulfillable. Abu Yusuf argues that even if impossible, the oath obligates expiation as a substitute. This lesson unpacks their proofs and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
A person swears to drink specific water from a jug; either there is no water initially or the water is spilled before the deadline. What is the ruling on breach?
2
State the two positions
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, no breach occurs because the act was impossible from the start or became impossible; the oath is void. According to Abu Yusuf, the oath is valid and breach occurs at the end of the day, requiring expiation.
3
Locate the underlying principle
The condition of 'tassawur al-birr' (possibility of fulfillment) is required by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad for the validity and continuity of the oath. Abu Yusuf does not require this condition.
4
Analyze the proofs
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: Oaths are contracted for fulfillment (birr); if birr is impossible, the oath cannot be valid. The substitute (kaffara) depends on a valid original, which does not exist. Abu Yusuf: The oath can still be valid because it obligates kaffara as a substitute for the impossible act.
The Hanafi response uses the example of yamin ghamus (false oath) which does not entail kaffara.
5
Apply to absolute vs time-limited oaths
For time-limited oaths, Abu Yusuf says no breach until the end of time; for absolute oaths, breach occurs immediately. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that in both cases the oath becomes void if the act is impossible at the required time.
The text explains the reasoning for the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ قَالَ إِنْ لَمْ أَشْرَبِ الْمَاءَ الَّذِي فِي هَذَا الْكُوزِ الْيَوْمَ فَامْرَأَتُهُ طَالِقٌ وَلَيْسَ فِي الْكُوزِ مَاءٌ لَمْ يَحْنِثْ فَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِ مَاءٌ فَأُهْرِيقَ قَبْلَ اللَّيْلِ لَمْ يَحْنَثْ وَهَذَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ فِي ذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ يَعْنِي إِذَا مَضَى الْيَوْمُ وَعَلَى هَذَا الْخِلَافِ إِذَا كَانَ الْيَمِينُ بِاللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَأَصْلُهُ أَنَّ شَرْطَ انْعِقَادِ الْيَمِينِ وَبَقَائِهِ التَّصَوُّرُ عِنْدَهُمَا خِلَافًا لِأَبِي يُوسُفَ لِأَنَّ الْيَمِينَ إِنَّمَا تُعْقَدُ لِلْبِرِّ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ تَصَوُّرِ الْبِرِّ لِيُمْكِنَ إِيجَابُهُ وَلَهُ أَنَّهُ أَمْكَنَ الْقَوْلُ بِالِانْعِقَادِ مُوجِبًا لِلْبِرِّ عَلَى وَجْهٍ يَظْهَرُ فِي حَقِّ الْخَلْفِ وَهُوَ الْكَفَّارَةُ قُلْنَا لَا بُدَّ مِنْ تَصَوُّرِ الْأَصْلِ لِيَنْعَقِدَ فِي حَقِّ الْخَلْفِ وَهَذَا لَا يَنْعَقِدُ الْغُمُوسُ مُوجِبًا لِلْكَفَّارَةِ وَلَوْ كَانَتِ الْيَمِينُ مُطْلَقَةً فَفِي الْوَجْهِ الْأَوَّلِ لَا يَحْنَثُ عِنْدَهُمَا وَعِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ يَحْنَثُ فِي الْحَالِ وَفِي الْوَجْهِ الثَّانِي يَحْنَثُ فِي قَوْلِهِمْ جَمِيعًا فَأَبُو يُوسُفَ فَرَّقَ بَيْنَ الْمُطْلَقِ وَالْمُوَقَّتِ وَوَجْهُ الْفَرْقِ أَنَّ التَّوْقِيتَ لِلتَّوَسُّعَةِ فَلَا يَجِبُ الْفِعْلُ إِلَّا فِي آخِرِ الْوَقْتِ فَلَا يَحْنَثُ قَبْلُ وَفِي الْمُطْلَقِ يَجِبُ الْبِرُّ كَمَا فَرَغَ وَقَدْ عَجَزَ فَيَحْنَثُ فِي الْحَالِ وَهُمَا فَرَّقَا بَيْنَهُمَا وَوَجْهُ الْفَرْقِ أَنَّ فِي الْمُطْلَقِ يَجِبُ الْبِرُّ كَمَا فَرَغَ فَإِذَا فَاتَ الْبِرُّ بِفَوَاتِ مَا عُقِدَ عَلَيْهِ الْيَمِينُ يَحْنَثُ فِي يَمِينِهِ كَمَا إِذَا مَاتَ الْحَالِفُ وَالْمَاءُ بَاقٍ أَمَّا فِي الْمُوَقَّتِ يَجِبُ الْبِرُّ فِي الْجُزْءِ الْآخِيرِ مِنَ الْوَقْتِ وَعِنْدَهُ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يَبْقَ مَحَلِّيَّةُ الْبِرِّ لِعَدَمِ التَّصَوُّرِ فَلَا يَجِبُ الْبِرُّ فِيهِ وَتَبْطُلُ الْيَمِينُ كَمَا إِذَا عَقَدَهُ ابْتِدَاءً فِي هَذِهِ الْحَالَةِ
And whoever says, 'If I do not drink the water that is in this jug today, then my wife is divorced,' and there is no water in the jug, he does not break his oath. If there is water in it and it is spilled before night, he does not break his oath. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said regarding all of this: i.e., when the day passes, he breaks his oath. And the same disagreement applies if the oath is by Allah Almighty. The foundation is that the condition for the validity and continuity of the oath is possibility (tassawur) according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf, because the oath is only made for fulfillment (birr), so fulfillment must be possible to be obligatory. For Abu Yusuf: It is possible to say that it is valid as entailing fulfillment in a way that appears in the substitute, which is the expiation (kaffara). We say: The original must be possible to be valid for the substitute, and this does not validate an oath of al-gumus (false oath) as entailing expiation. And if the oath is absolute, in the first scenario they say he does not break, and according to Abu Yusuf he breaks immediately. In the second scenario, he breaks according to all of them. So Abu Yusuf differentiates between absolute and time-limited oaths. The face of the difference: Time limitation allows expansion, so the act is only obligatory at the end of the time, so he does not break before. In the absolute, fulfillment is obligatory as soon as he finishes, and he is unable, so he breaks immediately. And they (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) differentiated between them. The face of the difference: In the absolute, fulfillment is obligatory as soon as he finishes; so when fulfillment is lost by the loss of what the oath was contracted upon, he breaks his oath, like when the swearer dies and the water remains. As for the time-limited, fulfillment is obligatory in the last part of the time, and at that point there remains no place for fulfillment due to lack of possibility, so fulfillment is not obligatory in it, and the oath becomes invalid, like when he contracts it initially in this situation.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage addresses a complex oath scenario and the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the condition of possibility (tassawur). The case: a person swears, 'If I do not drink the water in this jug today, my wife is divorced.' Three scenarios: (1) There is no water in the jug initially. (2) There is water but it is spilled before night. (3) There is water and it remains. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, in scenarios (1) and (2), no oath-break occurs because from the start or by the end of the day, the act of drinking that specific water is impossible. Abu Yusuf disagrees: he says the person breaks the oath when the day passes, because the oath was validly contracted and the person failed to fulfill it; he must pay expiation (kaffara) as a substitute. The underlying principle (asl): Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require that the object of the oath (birr) be possible (mutasawwar) at the time of the oath and continue to be possible throughout. Since possibility is a condition for validity and continuation of the oath, if it is impossible from the start, the oath never validly contracts; if it becomes impossible later, the oath becomes void. Abu Yusuf argues that even if the original act is impossible, the oath can still be validly contracted because it obligates a substitute (kaffara). The response: The substitute (khalaf) cannot exist without a valid original (asl). A false oath (yamīn ghamūs) does not necessitate expiation, so impossibility cannot be remedied by kaffara. The text then distinguishes between absolute oaths (muṭlaq) and time-limited oaths (muwaqqat). For time-limited oaths, Abu Yusuf rules that no breach occurs until the end of the time, because the obligation is only at the last moment. For absolute oaths, he says breach occurs immediately upon impossibility. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule that in absolute oaths, since the fulfillment is required immediately, if the object is lost (e.g., water disappears), the oath becomes void and no breach occurs. In time-limited oaths, the obligation is only at the last moment; if at that moment the object is impossible, the oath is void because it never had a valid object at the required time.

Key Terms
تَصَوُّر الْبِرّ (taṣawwur al-birr): The possibility or conceivability of fulfilling the oath; the sworn act must be possible at the time of the oath and remain so.
خَلْف / الْكَفَّارَة (khalaf / al-kaffāra): Substitute or successor; here referring to expiation (kaffara) as a replacement for the impossible sworn act.
يَمِين غَمُوس (yamīn ghamūs): A false oath about the past (like lying under oath), which does not require expiation in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if someone swears 'If I don't drink the water in this jug today' and there is no water from the start, what happens?
A) He breaks the oath at the end of the day and must pay expiation.
B) He does not break the oath because the oath was never validly contracted.
C) He must drink water from another jug to fulfill the oath.
D) The oath is suspended until water appears.

Key Takeaway
For an oath to be valid in the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), the sworn act must be possible at the time of the oath and at the required time; otherwise the oath is void.

Oath to Perform Habitually Impossible Acts
Ruling on oath to do something habitually impossible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on oaths involving habitual impossibility, distinguish it from absolute impossibility, and apply the rule to analogous cases.

Core Idea
An oath to do what is habitually impossible is valid if the act is possible in reality.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of oaths to perform acts that are habitually impossible but not absolutely impossible, such as climbing to the sky or turning a stone into gold. The majority of Hanafi imams hold the oath valid, while Imam Zufar disagrees. Understanding the distinction between habitual and absolute impossibility is key to determining the oath's validity and the swearer's liability for expiation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Identify the ruling given by al-Quduri in the matn: the oath is valid and the swearer becomes sinful immediately after swearing.
Majority = Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Identify the opposing view
State Imam Zufar's position: the oath is not valid because the acts are habitually impossible, akin to absolute impossibility.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyse the majority's proof
The majority argues that the acts are conceptually possible in reality: angels ascend to the sky, and Allah can transform stone into gold. Therefore, the oath is valid.
The proof is rational (dalil aqli), focusing on tasawwur al-birr.
4
Understand the application of habitual impossibility
The swearer becomes sinful because habitual impossibility is treated as a cause of sin, analogous to the case of death: a dead person does not return by habit, but it is possible (resurrection), so an oath to do something after death is valid and the swearer sins.
Distinguish from the cup case where the act was absolutely impossible.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to the majority, the swearer must pay expiation (kaffarah) for breaking the oath; according to Zufar, no expiation is required because the oath is invalid.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the majority view.

قَالَ وَمَنْ حَلَفَ لَيَصْعَدَنَّ السَّمَاءَ اَوْلَيُقَلَّبَنَّ هَذَا الْحَجَرَةَ هَبًا اِنْعَقَدَتْ يَمِينُهُ وَ حَنَثَ عَقِيْبَهَا وَقَالَ زُفَرُلَا تَنْعَقِدُ لأَنَّهُ مُسْتَحِيْلٌ عَادَةً فَاشْبَهَ الْمُسْتَحِيلَ حَقِيقَةٌ فَلَا يَنْعَقِدُ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْبَرَّ مُتَصَوَّرٌ حَقِيقَةٌ لِأَنَّ الصُّعُودَ إِلَى السَّمَاءِ مُمْكِن حَقِيقَةُ الاَتَرى اَنَّ الْمَلَائِكَةَ يَصْعَدُونَ السَّمَاءَ وَكَذَا تَحَوَّلَ الْحَجَرُ ذَهَبًا بِتَحْوِيْلِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَإِذَا كَانَ مُتَصَوّرًا يَنعَقِدُ الْيَمِينُ مُوجِبًا لِخَلْفِهِ ثُمَّ يَحْنِتُ بِحُكْمِ الْحَجَرَ الثَّابِتِ عَادَةً كَمَا إِذَا مَاتَ الْحَالِفُ فَإِنَّهُ يَحْنِتُ مَعَ احْتِمَالِ إِعَادَةِ الْحَيَوةِ بِخِلَافِ مَسْأَلَةِ الْكُوزِ لِاَدَّ شُرْبَ الْمَاءِ الَّذِي فِي الْكُوزِ وَقْتَ الْحَلْفِ وَلَامَاءَ فِيهِ لَا يَتَصَوَّرُ فَلَمْ يَنعَقِدُ
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ میں آسمان پر ضرور چڑھ جاؤں گایا اس پتھر کو سونے سے بدل دوں گا تو اس کی قسم صحیح ہو جائے گی مگر قسم کے بعد حانث ہو جائے گا اور امام زفر نے فرمایا ہے کہ منعقد نہیں ہوگی۔ کیونکہ آسمان پر چڑھنا۔ اور پتھر کا سونے سے بدل جانا عادتا محال ہوتا ہے۔ اس بناء پر حقیقی محال کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ اس لئے قسم منعقد نہیں ہوگی اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس قسم کو پورا کرنے کا تصور کرناممکن ہے کیونکہ آسمان پر چڑھنا حقیقت میں بھی ممکن ہے۔ کیا یہ نہیں دیکھتے کہ فرشتے آسمان پر چڑھ جاتے ہیں۔ اسی طرح اللہ تعالیٰ پتھر کو سونا بنادے تو اس
He (al-Quduri) said: Whoever swears 'I will certainly ascend to the sky' or 'I will certainly turn this stone into gold', his oath is valid and he becomes sinful immediately after it. Zufar said: It is not valid because it is habitually impossible, so it resembles something impossible in reality, so it is not valid. Our proof is that fulfillment is conceptually possible in reality because ascending to the sky is possible in reality—do you not see that angels ascend to the sky? Similarly, the transformation of stone into gold is by the transformation of Allah the Exalted. And when it is conceptually possible, the oath is valid, making a substitute obligatory, then he becomes sinful by the ruling of the habitual impossibility, just as when the swearer dies, he becomes sinful despite the possibility of life being restored. Unlike the case of the cup, because drinking the water that was in the cup at the time of the oath, and there was no water in it, is not conceivable, so it was not valid.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding oaths to perform acts that are habitually impossible but not absolutely impossible. The matn from al-Quduri states that if someone swears to climb to the sky or to turn a stone into gold, the oath is valid and he becomes sinful immediately after swearing. Imam Zufar disagrees, arguing that since these actions are habitually impossible, the oath is not valid. The Hanafi response is that both actions are conceptually possible in reality: ascending to the sky is possible (as angels do), and Allah can transform a stone into gold. Therefore, the oath is valid. The person becomes sinful because habitual impossibility is treated as a cause of sin, similar to the case where a swearer dies – he becomes sinful despite the possibility of resurrection, because the habit is that a dead person does not return. This case is distinguished from the earlier cup case: in the cup case, at the time of swearing there was no water at all, so the act was absolutely impossible; here, the acts are possible in reality even if uncommon. The Urdu commentary explains that the oath is valid and the swearer becomes sinful immediately because the action is conceivable, though habitually impossible.

Key Terms
مستحيل عادة (mustahil 'ādatan): Habitually impossible; something that does not occur in normal experience but is not absolutely impossible in reality.
تصور البر (tasawwur al-birr): Conceptual possibility of fulfillment; the act sworn must be conceivable in reality.
حنث (hanath): Breaking the oath; becoming sinful by failing to fulfill the sworn act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), if someone swears to climb to the sky, what is the ruling?
A) The oath is not valid because climbing to the sky is impossible.
B) The oath is valid and he becomes sinful immediately.
C) The oath is valid but he does not become sinful until the end of his life.
D) The oath is not valid unless he explicitly mentions a time limit.

Key Takeaway
An oath is valid if the sworn act is possible in reality, even if habitually impossible; only absolute impossibility invalidates the oath.
